<p><b>Brian Harold May</b>, <span style="font-size:85%;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (born 19 July 1947) is an English musician, singer, songwriter and astrophysicist best known as the lead guitarist of the rock band <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>. He uses a home-built electric guitar, called the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>. His compositions for the band include "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Bottomed_Girls" title="Fat Bottomed Girls">Fat Bottomed Girls</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flash_(Queen_song)" title="Flash (Queen song)">Flash</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">Save Me</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>".</p>
<p>May was a co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> with lead singer <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a> and drummer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a>, having previously performed with Taylor in the band <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile</a>, which he had joined while he was at university. Within five years of their formation in 1970 and the recruitment of bass player <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">John Deacon</a> completing the lineup, Queen had become established as one of the biggest rock bands in Britain with the album <i><a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">A Night at the Opera</a></i> and its single "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>". From the mid-1970s until the early 1990s, Queen were an almost constant presence in the UK charts and played some of the biggest venues in the world, most notably giving an acclaimed performance at <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> in 1985. As a member of Queen, May became regarded as a virtuoso musician, and he was identified with a distinctive sound created through his layered guitar work. Following the death of Mercury in 1991, Queen were put on hiatus for several years but were eventually reconvened by May and Taylor for further performances featuring other vocalists. In 2005, a <a href="/wiki/Planet_Rock_(radio_station)" title="Planet Rock (radio station)">Planet Rock</a> poll saw May voted the 7th greatest guitarist of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> He was ranked at No. 26 on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine's list of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_greatest_guitarists_of_all_time" title="Rolling Stone's 100 greatest guitarists of all time">100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2012, May was ranked the 2nd greatest guitarist of all time by a <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_World" title="Guitar World">Guitar World</a></i> magazine readers poll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was appointed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Most_Excellent_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) in 2005 for "services to the music industry and for charity work".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> May attained a PhD in <a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">astrophysics</a> from <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a> in 2007 and was <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Liverpool_John_Moores_University" title="Chancellor of Liverpool John Moores University">Chancellor of Liverpool John Moores University</a> from 2008 to 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-5">[5]</a></sup> He was a "science team collaborator" with NASA's <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a> Pluto mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> He is also a co-founder of the awareness campaign, <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_Day" title="Asteroid Day">Asteroid Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian-2016_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-2016-8">[8]</a></sup> Asteroid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/52665_Brianmay" title="52665 Brianmay">52665 Brianmay</a> was named after him. May is also an animal rights activist, campaigning against the hunting of foxes and the culling of badgers in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animal_rights_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-animal_rights-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Brian Harold May, the only child of Harold and Ruth May, was born in <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_London" title="Hampton, London">Hampton, London</a> on 19 July 1947, and attended the local Hampton Grammar School, then a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voluntary_aided" title="Voluntary aided">voluntary aided</a> school (now <a href="/wiki/Independent_school" title="Independent school">independent</a> and known as <a href="/wiki/Hampton_School" title="Hampton School">Hampton School</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> He is of English and Scottish descent, with his mother being Scots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> During this time, he formed his first band, named 1984 after <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">novel of the same name</a>, with vocalist and bassist <a href="/wiki/Tim_Staffell" title="Tim Staffell">Tim Staffell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rcnov95_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-rcnov95-13">[13]</a></sup> At Hampton Grammar School, he attained ten <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Education" title="General Certificate of Education">GCE</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O-Level" title="O-Level">Ordinary Levels</a> and three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-Level" title="A-Level">A-Levels</a> (Physics, Mathematics and Applied Mathematics).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rcnov95_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-rcnov95-13">[13]</a></sup> He studied Mathematics and Physics at <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, graduating with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">BSc.</a> in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> with honours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Musical career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1968.E2.80.931970:_Smile">1968â1970: Smile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1968â1970: Smile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile (band)</a></div>
<p>May formed the band Smile in 1968. The group included <a href="/wiki/Tim_Staffell" title="Tim Staffell">Tim Staffell</a> as the lead singer and bassist, and later, drummer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a>, who also went on to play for <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>. The band lasted for only two years, from 1968 to 1970, as Staffell departed in 1970, leaving the band with a catalogue of nine songs. Smile would reunite for several songs on 22 December 1992. Taylor's band <a href="/wiki/The_Cross_(band)" title="The Cross (band)">The Cross</a> were headliners, and he brought May and Staffell on to play "Earth" and "If I Were a Carpenter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> May also performed several other songs that night.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970.E2.80.93present:_Queen">1970âpresent: Queen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970âpresent: Queen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen (band)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hannover7907.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="600" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hannover7907.jpg/220px-Hannover7907.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hannover7907.jpg/330px-Hannover7907.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hannover7907.jpg/440px-Hannover7907.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hannover7907.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May (right) on stage with Queen in 1979.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Queen's three-part vocal harmonies, May was generally the lower-range backing vocalist. On some of his songs, he sings the lead vocals, most notably the first verse of "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>", the final verse of "<a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven#.22Mother_Love.22" title="Made in Heaven">Mother Love</a>", the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_eight" title="Middle eight">middle eight</a> on "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>" and "Flash's Theme", and full lead vocals on "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Some_Day_One_Day" title="Some Day One Day">Some Day One Day</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack_(album)#She_Makes_Me_.28Stormtrooper_in_Stilettoes.29" title="Sheer Heart Attack (album)">She Makes Me (Stormtrooper in Stilettoes)</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2739_(Queen_song)" title="'39 (Queen song)">'39</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Good_Company_(Queen_song)" title="Good Company (Queen song)">Good Company</a>", "<a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_(album)#Long_Away" title="A Day at the Races (album)">Long Away</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_Dead,_All_Dead" title="All Dead, All Dead">All Dead, All Dead</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleeping_on_the_Sidewalk" title="Sleeping on the Sidewalk">Sleeping on the Sidewalk</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Jazz_(Queen_album)#Leaving_Home_Ain.27t_Easy" title="Jazz (Queen album)">Leaving Home Ain't Easy</a>" and "Sail Away Sweet Sister".</p>
<p>Throughout Queen's career, May frequently wrote songs for the band and has composed many worldwide hits such as "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Bottomed_Girls" title="Fat Bottomed Girls">Fat Bottomed Girls</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Who_Wants_To_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants To Live Forever">Who Wants To Live Forever</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>" as well as writing significant hit songs "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flash_(Queen_song)" title="Flash (Queen song)">Flash</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Now_I%27m_Here" title="Now I'm Here">Now I'm Here</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack#.22Brighton_Rock.22" title="Sheer Heart Attack">Brighton Rock</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Prophet%27s_Song" title="The Prophet's Song">The Prophet's Song</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Las_Palabras_de_Amor" title="Las Palabras de Amor">Las Palabras de Amor</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/No-One_But_You" title="No-One But You">No-One But You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">Save Me</a>". Typically, either Mercury or May wrote the most songs on every Queen album.</p>
<p>After the famous <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> concert in 1985, Mercury rang his band members and proposed writing a song together. The result was "<a href="/wiki/One_Vision" title="One Vision">One Vision</a>", which was basically May on music (the <i>Magic Years</i> documentary shows how he came up with the opening section and the basic guitar riff) and the lyrics were co-written by all four band members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>For their 1989 release album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Miracle_(album)" title="The Miracle (album)">The Miracle</a></i>, the band had decided that all of the tracks would be credited to the entire band, no matter who had been the main writer. Still, interviews and musical analyses tend to help identify the input of each member on each track. May composed "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_It_All_(Queen_song)" title="I Want It All (Queen song)">I Want It All</a>" for that album, as well as "<a href="/wiki/Scandal_(song)" title="Scandal (song)">Scandal</a>" (based on his personal problems with the British press). For the rest of the album he did not contribute so much creatively, although he helped in building the basis of "Party" and "Was It All Worth It" (both being predominantly Mercury's pieces) and created the guitar riff of "Chinese Torture".</p>
<p>Queen's subsequent album was <i><a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(album)" title="Innuendo (album)">Innuendo</a></i>, on which May's contributions increased, although more in arrangements than actual writing in most cases; for the <a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(song)" title="Innuendo (song)">title track</a> he did some of the arrangement for the heavy solo, then he added vocal harmonies to "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Going_Slightly_Mad" title="I'm Going Slightly Mad">I'm Going Slightly Mad</a>" and composed the solo of "<a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">These Are the Days of Our Lives</a>", a song for which the four of them decided the keyboard parts together. He changed the tempo and key of Mercury's song "The Hitman" and took it under his wing, even singing guide vocal in the demo. May also co-wrote some of the guitar lines in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bijou_(Queen_song)" title="Bijou (Queen song)">Bijou</a>".</p>
<p>Two songs that May had composed for his first solo album, "<a href="/wiki/Headlong_(song)" title="Headlong (song)">Headlong</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Live_With_You" title="I Can't Live With You">I Can't Live With You</a>", eventually ended up in the Queen project. His other composition was "<a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">The Show Must Go On</a>", a group effort in which he was the coordinator and primary composer, but in which they all had input, Deacon and Taylor with the famous chord sequence. In recent years, he has supervised the remastering of Queen albums and various DVD and greatest hits releases. In 2004, he announced that he and drummer Roger Taylor were going on tour for the first time in 18Â years as "Queen", along with <a href="/wiki/Free_(band)" title="Free (band)">Free</a>/<a href="/wiki/Bad_Company" title="Bad Company">Bad Company</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a>. Billed as "<a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a>", the band played throughout 2005 and 2006 in South Africa, Europe, Aruba, Japan, and North America and released a new album with Paul Rodgers in 2008, entitled <i>The Cosmos Rocks</i>. This album was supported by a major tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Paul Rodgers then left the band <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> in May 2009 and it wasn't until 2011 that another vocalist, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>was recruited. They subsequently went on a <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert_Tour_2012" title="Queen + Adam Lambert Tour 2012">2012 European Tour</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert_Tour_2014%E2%80%932015" title="Queen + Adam Lambert Tour 2014â2015">world tour over 2014 and 2015</a> and, most recently, <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert_2016_Summer_Festival_Tour" title="Queen + Adam Lambert 2016 Summer Festival Tour">2016 Festival Tour</a>. They also famously played the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert_Rock_Big_Ben_Live" title="Queen + Adam Lambert Rock Big Ben Live">Big Ben New Year concert</a> on New Year's Eve 2014 and New Year's Day 2015.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1983.E2.80.931998:_The_Brian_May_band">1983â1998: The Brian May band</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1983â1998: The Brian May band">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brianrs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="558" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/170px-Brianrs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/255px-Brianrs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Brianrs.jpg/340px-Brianrs.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brianrs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May in 1981 with the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During 1983, several members of Queen explored side projects. On 21 and 22 April in Los Angeles, May was in the studio with Eddie Van Halen, with no intentions of recording anything; the result of those days was a mini album entitled '<a href="/wiki/Star_Fleet_Project" title="Star Fleet Project">Star Fleet Project</a>', which originally wasn't going to be released.</p>
<p>May contributed to former <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a> guitarist <a href="/wiki/Steve_Hackett" title="Steve Hackett">Steve Hackett</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Feedback_86" title="Feedback 86">Feedback 86</a></i>, playing guitar on the track "Cassandra" and providing guitar and vocals for "Slot Machine," which was co-written by May. Although produced in 1986, the album was not issued as a commercial release until 2000. May worked with his second wife <a href="/wiki/Anita_Dobson" title="Anita Dobson">Anita Dobson</a> on her first album, in which she sang vocals to the <i><a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a></i> theme tune. In this form, the tune became the song "<a href="/wiki/Anyone_Can_Fall_in_Love" title="Anyone Can Fall in Love">Anyone Can Fall in Love</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> May produced the song, which reached No. 4 in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> in August 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1989, May contributed guitar solos to the song "When Death Calls" on <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>'s 14th album <i><a href="/wiki/Headless_Cross" title="Headless Cross">Headless Cross</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Living_in_a_Box" title="Living in a Box">Living in a Box</a> track "Blow The House Down" from the album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gatecrashing" title="Gatecrashing">Gatecrashing</a></i>.</p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>After the tragic break-up of any band, it feels impossible to continue but I was really glad that Brian did launch a solo career. He had such a lot of music in him and a great deal more to give</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Â â<a href="/wiki/Joe_Satriani" title="Joe Satriani">Joe Satriani</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011-23">[23]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>In the aftermath of the November 1991 death of <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, May chose to deal with his grief by committing himself as fully as possible to work, first by finishing his solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Light" title="Back to the Light">Back to the Light</a></i>, and then touring worldwide to promote it. He frequently remarked in press interviews that this was the only form of self-prescribed therapy he could think of.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Joe_Elliott" title="Joe Elliott">Joe Elliott</a>, "It was undoubtedly an enormous and terrible blow to lose someone he was so close to. Personally, I know it ripped the heart out of Brian, but having said that, he was in great spirits after the album was finished."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late 1992, <a href="/wiki/The_Brian_May_Band" title="The Brian May Band">the Brian May Band</a> was officially formed. An earlier version of the band was loosely formed for 19 October 1991, the date of the band's last concert of reunion, when May took part in the <i>Guitar Legends</i> guitar festival in <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, Spain. The line-up for his performance was May on vocals and lead guitar, <a href="/wiki/Cozy_Powell" title="Cozy Powell">Cozy Powell</a> on drums and percussion, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Moran_(music_producer)" title="Mike Moran (music producer)">Mike Moran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Wakeman" title="Rick Wakeman">Rick Wakeman</a> on keyboards, and <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Ryder" title="Maggie Ryder">Maggie Ryder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miriam_Stockley" title="Miriam Stockley">Miriam Stockley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Thompson_(English_musician)" title="Chris Thompson (English musician)">Chris Thompson</a> on backing vocals. The original line-up was May on vocals and lead guitar, Powell on drums and percussion, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Casswell" title="Michael Casswell">Michael Casswell</a> on guitar, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Murray_(British_musician)" title="Neil Murray (British musician)">Neil Murray</a> on bass, and Ryder, Stockley and Thompson on backing vocals. This version of the band lasted only during the South American support tour (supporting <a href="/wiki/The_B-52%27s" title="The B-52's">The B-52's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cocker" title="Joe Cocker">Joe Cocker</a>) on only five dates.</p>
<p>Afterwards, May made significant changes, feeling the group never quite gelled. May brought guitarist <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Moses" title="Jamie Moses">Jamie Moses</a> on board to replace Mike Caswell. The other change made was in the backing vocals department, when Ryder, Stockley and Thompson were replaced with <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Porter" title="Catherine Porter">Catherine Porter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shelley_Preston" title="Shelley Preston">Shelley Preston</a>. On 23 February 1993, this new line-up of The Brian May Band began its world tour in the US, both supporting <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a> and headlining a few dates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The tour would take them through North America, Europe (support act: Valentine) and Japan. After the tour ended on 18 December 1993, May returned to the studio with fellow surviving Queen band members <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Meddows-Taylor" title="Roger Meddows-Taylor">Roger Taylor</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">John Deacon</a> to work on tracks that became <i><a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven" title="Made in Heaven">Made in Heaven</a></i>, the final Queen studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buckley_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley-26">[26]</a></sup> The band took Mercury's solo album demos and last recordings, which he managed to perform in the studio after the album <i><a href="/wiki/Innuendo_(album)" title="Innuendo (album)">Innuendo</a></i> was finished, and completed them with their additions both musically and vocally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Work on the album after Mercury's death originally began in 1992 by Deacon and May, but was left until a later date, due to other commitments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buckley_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995, May began working towards a new solo album of covers tentatively named <i>Heroes</i>, in addition to working on various film and television projects and other collaborations. May subsequently changed the approach from covers to focus on those collaborations and on new material. The songs included <i><a href="/wiki/Another_World_(Brian_May_album)" title="Another World (Brian May album)">Another World</a></i>, and featured mainly <a href="/wiki/Spike_Edney" title="Spike Edney">Spike Edney</a>, Cozy Powell, Neil Murray and Jamie Moses. On 5 April 1998, Cozy Powell was killed in a car accident on the <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway" title="M4 motorway">M4 motorway</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, England. This caused a huge, unexpected disruption to the upcoming tour for The Brian May Band, with a new drummer being needed at short notice. <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ferrone" title="Steve Ferrone">Steve Ferrone</a> was brought on to help May finish recording drums and to join the band for the early stage promotional tour of five dates in Europe before the world tour. Following the early promotional tour, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Singer" title="Eric Singer">Eric Singer</a> replaced Steve Ferrone for the full 1998 world tour.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.E2.80.93present">2000âpresent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000âpresent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="1224" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Brian_May.JPG/180px-Brian_May.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Brian_May.JPG/270px-Brian_May.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Brian_May.JPG/360px-Brian_May.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May performing in Chile, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From his last solo release in 1998, May has been performing as a solo artist, as part of an ensemble, and infrequently as Queen with <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a>. On 22 October 2000, Brian May made a guest appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="MotÃ¶rhead">MotÃ¶rhead</a> 25th Anniversary show at <a href="/wiki/Brixton_Academy" title="Brixton Academy">Brixton Academy</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Clarke" title="Eddie Clarke">Eddie Clarke</a> (former MotÃ¶rhead guitarist) for the encore song "<a href="/wiki/Overkill_(Mot%C3%B6rhead_song)" title="Overkill (MotÃ¶rhead song)">Overkill</a>". As part of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II</a> celebrations in June 2002, May performed a <a href="/wiki/Guitar_solo" title="Guitar solo">guitar solo</a> of "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a>" from the roof of <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, with the performance appearing on the 30th Anniversary DVD edition of <i>A Night at the Opera</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In 2004 May played guitar on the song "Someone to Die For" on the <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2_(soundtrack)" title="Spider-Man 2 (soundtrack)">soundtrack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In the Queen's birthday honours list of 2005, he was made a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Most_Excellent_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Commander of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Most Excellent Order of the British Empire</a> "for services to the music industry and for charity work".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>May was a celebrity guest at the <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a> reunion concert at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> May and Genesis frontman <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a> had worked together on two previous occasions, at <a href="/wiki/The_Prince%27s_Trust" title="The Prince's Trust">The Prince's Trust</a> Rock Gala in 1988 and the <a href="/wiki/Party_at_the_Palace" title="Party at the Palace">Party at the Palace</a> in 2002, when Collins had played drums with Queen. In 2011 he contributed to a feature about Collins for <i><a href="/wiki/FHM" title="FHM">FHM</a></i>, praising him as "a great guy and an amazing drummer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>May worked extensively with stage actress and singer <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Ellis" title="Kerry Ellis">Kerry Ellis</a>, after he cast her in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You_(musical)" title="We Will Rock You (musical)">We Will Rock You</a></i>. He produced and arranged her debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Anthems_(Kerry_Ellis_album)" title="Anthems (Kerry Ellis album)">Anthems</a></i> (2010), a follow-up to her extended play <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_in_Rock" title="Wicked in Rock">Wicked in Rock</a></i> (2008), as well as appearing with Ellis at many public performancesÂ â playing guitar alongside her. He also contributed a guitar solo to <a href="/wiki/Meat_Loaf" title="Meat Loaf">Meat Loaf</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hang_Cool,_Teddy_Bear" title="Hang Cool, Teddy Bear">Hang Cool, Teddy Bear</a></i> album in exchange for the use of drummer <a href="/wiki/John_Miceli" title="John Miceli">John Miceli</a>. Along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elena_Vidal" title="Elena Vidal">Elena Vidal</a>, Brian May released a historical book in 2009 entitled <i><a href="/wiki/A_Village_Lost_and_Found" title="A Village Lost and Found">A Village Lost and Found: Scenes in Our Village</a></i>. The book is an annotated collection of stereoscopic photographs taken by the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> photographer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Richard_Williams" title="Thomas Richard Williams">T. R. Williams</a> and it is sold with a focussing stereoscope. May became an enthusiast of stereoscope photographs as a child, and first encountered the work of Williams during the late 1960s. In 2003, May announced a search to identify the actual location of the <i>Scenes in Our Village</i> images. In 2004 May reported that he had identified the location as the village of <a href="/wiki/Hinton_Waldrist" title="Hinton Waldrist">Hinton Waldrist</a> in Oxfordshire.</p>
<p>On 20 May 2009, May and Queen band mate Roger Taylor performed "We Are the Champions" live on the season finale of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> with winner <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a> and runner-up <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> providing a vocal duet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIdol_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIdol-34">[34]</a></sup> In November 2009, May appeared with Taylor on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i>, with Queen mentoring the contestants, then later performing "Bohemian Rhapsody". In April 2010, May founded the "Save Me" 2010 project to work against any proposed repeal of the British fox-hunting ban, and also to promote animal rights in Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-save-me.org.uk_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-save-me.org.uk-35">[35]</a></sup> In February 2011 it was announced that May would tour with <a href="/wiki/Kerry_Ellis" title="Kerry Ellis">Kerry Ellis</a>, playing 12 dates across the UK in May 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> On 1 March 2013 May and Ellis played a free thirty-minute acoustic set at <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras railway station</a> to launch Tiger Track, a three-week tiger conservation event.</p>
<p>On 18 April 2011, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> confirmed that May would play guitar on her track "<a href="/wiki/You_and_I_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="You and I (Lady Gaga song)">You and I</a>" from her latest album <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i>, released on 23 May 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In June 2011, May performed with <a href="/wiki/Tangerine_Dream" title="Tangerine Dream">Tangerine Dream</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Starmus_Festival" title="Starmus Festival">Starmus Festival</a> on <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, celebrating the 50th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a>'s first spaceflight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 August, May performed "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Black_Parade" title="Welcome to the Black Parade">Welcome to the Black Parade</a>" with American rock band <a href="/wiki/My_Chemical_Romance" title="My Chemical Romance">My Chemical Romance</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reading_Festival" title="Reading Festival">Reading Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> On 28 August, May performed "You and I" live with Lady Gaga at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a> at the Nokia Theatre, Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On 10 October, May made an appearance to celebrate the reunion of British rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Darkness_(band)" title="The Darkness (band)">The Darkness</a> at an "intimate" <a href="/wiki/100_Club" title="100 Club">100 Club</a> show with support from <a href="/wiki/Dark_Stares" title="Dark Stares">Dark Stares</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Darkness_Wow_The_100_Club_At_Intimate_Show_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Darkness_Wow_The_100_Club_At_Intimate_Show-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Darkness_.40_100_Club_10_October_2011_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Darkness_.40_100_Club_10_October_2011-42">[42]</a></sup> A long-time fan of the group, May performed three songs onstage with The Darkness, including Queen's "<a href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down" title="Tie Your Mother Down">Tie Your Mother Down</a>", at the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a> on their subsequent "comeback" tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Guitarist_Brian_May_Joins_The_Darkness_On_Stage_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Guitarist_Brian_May_Joins_The_Darkness_On_Stage-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QUEEN.27s_BRIAN_MAY_Performs_With_THE_DARKNESS_In_London_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-QUEEN.27s_BRIAN_MAY_Performs_With_THE_DARKNESS_In_London-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Europe Music Awards">2011 MTV Europe Music Awards</a> on 6 November, Queen received the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award_for_Global_Icon" title="MTV Europe Music Award for Global Icon">Global Icon Award</a>, which <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> presented to Brian May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-45">[45]</a></sup> Queen closed the awards ceremony, with <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> on vocals, performing "The Show Must Go On", "We Will Rock You" and "We Are the Champions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EMA_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-EMA-45">[45]</a></sup> The collaboration garnered a positive response from both fans and critics, resulting in speculation about future projects together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-46">[46]</a></sup> Queen + Adam Lambert played two shows at the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a>, London on 11 and 12 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Both shows sold out within 24 hours of tickets going on open sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> A third London date was added for 14 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> On 30 June, Queen + Lambert performed in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, Ukraine at a joint concert with <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> for the Elena Pinchuk ANTIAIDS Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Queen also performed with Lambert on 3 July 2012 at Moscow's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Moscow)" title="Olympic Stadium (Moscow)">Olympic Stadium</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and on 7 July 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Stadion_Miejski_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Stadion Miejski (WrocÅaw)">Municipal Stadium</a> in Wroclaw, Poland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012, May featured on <a href="/wiki/N-Dubz" title="N-Dubz">N-Dubz</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Dappy" title="Dappy">Dappy</a>'s solo single "<a href="/wiki/Rockstar_(Dappy_song)" title="Rockstar (Dappy song)">Rockstar</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dappy_.27pays_tribute_to_Amy_Winehouse.27_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dappy_.27pays_tribute_to_Amy_Winehouse.27-55">[55]</a></sup> providing "rumbling guitar riffs which culminate in an electrifying solo".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27Rockstar.27_-_Single_review_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27Rockstar.27_-_Single_review-56">[56]</a></sup> The pair also collaborated on a performance of "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Live_Lounge" title="Live Lounge">Live Lounge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dappy_Will_Rock_You_in_the_Live_Lounge_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dappy_Will_Rock_You_in_the_Live_Lounge-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 August 2012, Queen performed at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics2012_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics2012-58">[58]</a></sup> May performed part of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_Rock_(song)" title="Brighton Rock (song)">Brighton Rock</a>" solo before being joined by Taylor and solo artist <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a> for a performance of "We Will Rock You".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics2012_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics2012-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> On 16 September 2012, May appeared at the Sunflower Jam charity concert at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, performing alongside bassist <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_(musician)" title="John Paul Jones (musician)">John Paul Jones</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>), drummer <a href="/wiki/Ian_Paice" title="Ian Paice">Ian Paice</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>), and vocalists <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">Bruce Dickinson</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Alice_Cooper" title="Alice Cooper">Alice Cooper</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>May donated his guitar talent to the end credits song from the film, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Dog_Named_Gucci" title="A Dog Named Gucci">A Dog Named Gucci</a></i>, in the song "One Voice", which also features the talents of <a href="/wiki/Norah_Jones" title="Norah Jones">Norah Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aimee_Mann" title="Aimee Mann">Aimee Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susanna_Hoffs" title="Susanna Hoffs">Susanna Hoffs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lydia_Loveless" title="Lydia Loveless">Lydia Loveless</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neko_Case" title="Neko Case">Neko Case</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_Calder" title="Kathryn Calder">Kathryn Calder</a>. It was produced by Dean Falcone, who also wrote the film's score. "One Voice" was released on <a href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day" title="Record Store Day">Record Store Day</a>, 16 April 2016, with profits from the sale of the single going to benefit animal charities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.932009:_Queen_.2B_Paul_Rodgers">2004â2009: Queen + Paul Rodgers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2004â2009: Queen + Paul Rodgers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="773" data-file-width="1024" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/220px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/330px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg/440px-2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2005_Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2005 <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of 2004, May and Taylor announced that they would reunite and return to touring in 2005, with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">Paul Rodgers</a> (founder and former lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Free_(band)" title="Free (band)">Free</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bad_Company" title="Bad Company">Bad Company</a>). Brian May's website also stated that Rodgers would be "featured with" Queen as <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">Queen + Paul Rodgers</a>, not replacing the late Freddie Mercury. The retired John Deacon would not be participating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bmcom_jdr_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-bmcom_jdr-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2005 and 2006 Queen and Paul Rodgers embarked on a <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">world tour</a>, the first leg being Europe and the second, Japan and the US in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen2006_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen2006-63">[63]</a></sup> On 25 May 2006, Queen received the inaugural <a href="/wiki/VH1_Rock_Honors" title="VH1 Rock Honors">VH1 Rock Honors</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay_Events_Center" title="Mandalay Bay Events Center">Mandalay Bay Events Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, Nevada, and May and Taylor were joined on stage with the <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a> to perform a selection of Queen songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen2006_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen2006-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On 15 August 2006, May confirmed through his website and fan club that Queen + Paul Rodgers would begin producing their first studio album beginning in October, to be recorded at a "secret location".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cosmos_Rocks" title="The Cosmos Rocks">The Cosmos Rocks</a></i>, was released in Europe on 12 September 2008 and in the United States on 28 October 2008. Following the album the band again embarked on a tour through Europe and parts of the US, opening on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_Square,_Kharkiv" title="Freedom Square, Kharkiv">Kharkov's freedom square</a> in front of 350,000 Ukrainian fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kharkov_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kharkov-66">[66]</a></sup> The show in Ukraine was later <a href="/wiki/Live_in_Ukraine" title="Live in Ukraine">released on DVD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kharkov_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kharkov-66">[66]</a></sup> Queen and Paul Rodgers officially split up on 12 May 2009. Rodgers does not rule out the possibility of working together again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Queen_.2B_Adam_Lambert">2011âpresent: Queen + Adam Lambert</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2011âpresent: Queen + Adam Lambert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert" title="Queen + Adam Lambert">Queen + Adam Lambert</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg/220px-Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg/330px-Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg/440px-Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adam_Lambert_and_Queen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert" title="Queen + Adam Lambert">Queen + Adam Lambert</a> concert at the <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a>, Boston in July 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Not long after performing with <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> finalists <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> during the programme's season finale in 2009, May and Taylor began contemplating the future of Queen after the group's amicable split with frontman Paul Rodgers. Two years later, at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Europe Music Awards">2011 MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, Queen was presented that year's Global Icon Award, accepted by May. As part of the broadcast, Queen performed a short set with Lambert, receiving an overwhelmingly welcoming response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-46">[46]</a></sup> Speculation regarding a collaboration with Lambert soon arose, with the three formally announcing a short summer tour of Europe in 2012, including three dates at the <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a> in London, as well as shows in Ukraine, Russia and Poland. As with the partnership with Paul Rodgers, <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">John Deacon</a> did not participate.</p>
<p>The collaboration was revived in 2013, when the three performed together at the <a href="/wiki/IHeartRadio_Music_Festival" title="IHeartRadio Music Festival">iHeartRadio Music Festival</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Hotel_%26_Casino" title="MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino">MGM Grand Hotel &amp; Casino</a> in Las Vegas on 20 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Five months later, May, Taylor and Lambert announced a 19-date summer tour of North America on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Due to ticket demand, five dates were soon added.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In May 2014, shows in Australia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and New Zealand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> were announced, along with festival performances in South Korea<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The tour was extended to the UK and greater Europe in early 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The group performed together in South America in September 2015, including Queen's first performance at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio</a> Festival since 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, the group embarked across Europe and Asia on the <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert_2016_Summer_Festival_Tour" title="Queen + Adam Lambert 2016 Summer Festival Tour">Queen + Adam Lambert 2016 Summer Festival Tour</a>. This included closing the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_Festival" title="Isle of Wight Festival">Isle of Wight Festival</a> in England on 12 June where they performed "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" as a tribute to the victims of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Orlando_nightclub_shooting" title="2016 Orlando nightclub shooting">mass shooting at a gay nightclub</a> in Orlando, Florida earlier that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> On 12 September they performed at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Park_Hayarkon" title="Park Hayarkon">Park Hayarkon</a> in Tel-Aviv, Israel for the first time in front of 58,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Though the collaboration remains active, there are currently no plans of recording a studio album, though the three are willing to do so in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Highlights">Highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_2005_1010016.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="764" data-file-width="870" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Queen_2005_1010016.JPG/220px-Queen_2005_1010016.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Queen_2005_1010016.JPG/330px-Queen_2005_1010016.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Queen_2005_1010016.JPG/440px-Queen_2005_1010016.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_2005_1010016.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May performing in Frankfurt in 2005.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brian May began composing in 1968 to 1969, and through the years he has collaborated with other songwriters, including Frank Musker, with whom he wrote "<a href="/wiki/Too_Much_Love_Will_Kill_You" title="Too Much Love Will Kill You">Too Much Love Will Kill You</a>", and with Elizabeth Lamers, whose music won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Award" title="Ivor Novello Award">Ivor Novello Award</a> for Best Song Musically &amp; Lyrically in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> A meticulous arranger, he focuses on multi-part harmonies, often more <a href="/wiki/Counterpoint" title="Counterpoint">contrapuntal</a> than parallel â a relative rarity for rock guitar. Examples are found in Queen's albums <i>A Night at the Opera</i> and <i>A Day at the Races</i>, where he arranged a jazz band for guitar mini-orchestra ("Good Company"), a vocal canon ("The Prophet's Song") and guitar and vocal counterpoints ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teo_Torriatte" title="Teo Torriatte">Teo Torriatte</a>").</p>
<p>May explored a wide variety of styles in guitar, including <a href="/wiki/Sweep_picking" title="Sweep picking">sweep picking</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Was_It_All_Worth_It" title="Was It All Worth It">Was It All Worth It</a>", "Chinese Torture"), <a href="/wiki/Tremolo" title="Tremolo">tremolo</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_Rock_(song)#Brighton_Rock" title="Brighton Rock (song)">Brighton Rock</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Crazy" title="Stone Cold Crazy">Stone Cold Crazy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Death_on_Two_Legs_(Dedicated_to...)" title="Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)">Death on Two Legs</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Lady_(Queen_song)" title="Sweet Lady (Queen song)">Sweet Lady</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Get_Down_Make_Love" title="Get Down Make Love">Get Down Make Love</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_Attack" title="Dragon Attack">Dragon Attack</a>"), <a href="/wiki/Tapping" title="Tapping">tapping</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bijou_(Queen_song)" title="Bijou (Queen song)">Bijou</a>", "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Late" title="It's Late">It's Late</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Resurrection" title="Resurrection">Resurrection</a>", "Cyborg", "Rain Must Fall", "Business", "China Belle", "I Was Born To Love You"), slide guitar ("Drowse", "Tie Your Mother Down"), <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Hendrix</a> sounding licks ("<a href="/wiki/Liar_(Queen_song)" title="Liar (Queen song)">Liar</a>", "Brighton Rock"), tape-delay ("Brighton Rock", "White Man") and melodic sequences ("<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Killer_Queen" title="Killer Queen">Killer Queen</a>", "<a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">These Are the Days of Our Lives</a>"). Some of his solos and orchestral parts were composed by <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, who then asked May to bring them to life ("Bicycle Race", "<a href="/wiki/Lazing_on_a_Sunday_Afternoon" title="Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon">Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon</a>", "Killer Queen", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Old_Fashioned_Lover_Boy" title="Good Old Fashioned Lover Boy">Good Old Fashioned Lover Boy</a>"). May also performed notable acoustic works, including the acoustic guitar live version of "<a href="/wiki/Love_of_My_Life_(Queen_song)" title="Love of My Life (Queen song)">Love of My Life</a>" from 1975's <i>A Night at the Opera</i>, the finger-picked solo of "White Queen" and the <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a>-influenced "'39".</p>
<p>In January 2007, the readers of <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_World" title="Guitar World">Guitar World</a></i> voted May's guitar solos "Bohemian Rhapsody", "Brighton Rock" into the "top 50 Greatest Guitar Solos of all time" ("Bohemian Rhapsody" was voted No. 20 and "Brighton Rock" was voted #41).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aided by the uniqueness of his guitarÂ â the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>Â â May was often able to create strange and unusual sound effects. For example, he was able to imitate an orchestra in the song "<a href="/wiki/Queen_II#Procession" title="Queen II">Procession</a>"; in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Get_Down,_Make_Love" title="Get Down, Make Love">Get Down, Make Love</a>" he was able to create various sound effects with his guitar; in "<a href="/wiki/Good_Company_(Queen_song)" title="Good Company (Queen song)">Good Company</a>" he used his guitar to mimic a trombone, a piccolo and several other instruments for the song's Dixieland jazz band feel. Queen used a "No synthesizers were used on this album" sleeve note on their early albums to make this clear to the listeners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> May also used his guitar to create the chime effect in Bohemian Rhapsody.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bohrapchimes_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-bohrapchimes-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_instruments">Other instruments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other instruments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first instrument May learned to play was the <a href="/wiki/Banjo_uke" title="Banjo uke">banjolele</a>, which he played on Queen's song "Bring Back That Leroy Brown" (live and in the studio). For "Good Company", he used a regular baritone ukulele which he had bought in Hawaii on a holiday. Occasionally, May would also record on other string instruments such as harp (one chord per take, then copied and pasted by the engineer to make it sound like a continuous performance) and bass (on some demos and many songs in his solo career, and the Queen + Paul Rodgers album).</p>
<p>As a child, he was also trained on classical piano. Although Freddie Mercury was the band's primary pianist, May would occasionally step in (such as on "<a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">Save Me</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Flash_(Queen_song)" title="Flash (Queen song)">Flash</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Who_Wants_To_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants To Live Forever">Who Wants To Live Forever</a>"). From 1979 onwards, he also played synthesisers, organ ("Wedding March", "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Live" title="Let Me Live">Let Me Live</a>") and programmed drum-machines for both Queen and outside projects (such as producing other artists and his own solo records).</p>
<p>May is also an accomplished singer. From Queen's <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_II" title="Queen II">Queen II</a></i> to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Game_(Queen_album)" title="The Game (Queen album)">The Game</a></i>, May contributed lead vocals to at least one song per album. May co-composed a mini-opera with <a href="/wiki/Lee_Holdridge" title="Lee Holdridge">Lee Holdridge</a>, <i>Il Colosso</i>, for <a href="/wiki/Steve_Barron" title="Steve Barron">Steve Barron</a>'s 1996 film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Pinocchio_(1996_film)" title="The Adventures of Pinocchio (1996 film)">The Adventures of Pinocchio</a></i>. May performed the opera with <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Hadley" title="Jerry Hadley">Jerry Hadley</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sissel_Kyrkjebo" title="Sissel Kyrkjebo">Sissel Kyrkjebo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Just_William" title="Just William">Just William</a>. On-screen, it was performed entirely by puppets.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicianship">Musicianship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Musicianship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="507" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg/170px-Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg/255px-Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg/340px-Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koeln1998_Brian_May.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May <a href="/wiki/Tapping" title="Tapping">tapping</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>He's a class act from head to toe, and it shows in his playing. I can listen to any player and pantomime their sound, but I can't do Brian May. He's just walking on higher ground.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Â â<a href="/wiki/Steve_Vai" title="Steve Vai">Steve Vai</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></cite></div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:10px;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>His tone immediately grabbed me. Brian has his own style and sound, so you can always tell his work. Even in 1971 he had incredible finesse, amazing fluidity.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">Â â<a href="/wiki/Andy_Powell" title="Andy Powell">Andy Powell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wishbone_Ash" title="Wishbone Ash">Wishbone Ash</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011-23">[23]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>May has been referred to as a virtuoso guitarist by many publications and musicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutcliffe_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sutcliffe-90">[90]</a></sup> He has featured in various music polls of great rock guitarists, and in 2011 was ranked number 26 on <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine's list of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_greatest_guitarists_of_all_time" title="Rolling Stone's 100 greatest guitarists of all time">100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-2">[2]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Van_Halen" title="Van Halen">Van Halen</a> vocalist <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Hagar" title="Sammy Hagar">Sammy Hagar</a> stated, "I thought Queen were really innovative and made some great sounding records.. I like the rockin' stuff. I think Brian May has one of the great guitar tones on the planet, and I really, really love his guitar work."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutcliffe_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sutcliffe-90">[90]</a></sup> May mainly used the "<a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>", which he designed when he was only 16Â years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rdspecial_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-rdspecial-91">[91]</a></sup> It was built with wood from an 18thÂ century fireplace. His comments on the guitar:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I like a big neck â thick, flat and wide. I lacquered the fingerboard with Rustin's Plastic Coating. The tremolo is interesting in that the arm's made from an old bicycle saddle bag carrier, the knob at the end's off a knitting needle and the springs are valve springs from an old motorbike.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>ââBrian May<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>In addition to using his home-made guitar he prefers to use coins (especially <a href="/wiki/Sixpence_(British_coin)" title="Sixpence (British coin)">a sixpence</a> from the farewell proof set of 1970), instead of a more traditional plastic <a href="/wiki/Plectrum" title="Plectrum">plectrum</a>, on the basis that their rigidity gives him more control in playing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-93">[93]</a></sup> He is known to carry coins in his pockets specifically for this purpose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>May's early influences were <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard" title="Cliff Richard">Cliff Richard</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Shadows" title="The Shadows">The Shadows</a>, who he says were "the most metallic thing(s) out at the time." Many years later he gained his opportunity to play on separate occasions with both Cliff Richard and Shadows lead guitarist <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a>. He has collaborated with Cliff Richard on a re-recording of the Cliff Richard and The Shadows (then known as The Drifters) 1958 hit "<a href="/wiki/Move_It" title="Move It">Move It</a>" on the Cliff Richard duets album <i>Two's Company</i> which was released on 6 November 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>May always stated that <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a> were the greatest influences on him. On 2 June 2010, on BBC Radio 2, Brian May said, "I would put <a href="/wiki/Rory_Gallagher" title="Rory Gallagher">Rory Gallagher</a> way up there; he is one of the people who inspired me most." On <i>Queen for an Hour</i> 1989 Interview on BBC RadioÂ 1, May listed <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> as his guitar heroes. In a 1991 interview for <i>Guitar World magazine</i>, May referred to <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a> as "my inspiration", and on seeing <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a> stated, "We used to look at those guys and think, "That's the way it should be done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> May told <i><a href="/wiki/Guitarist_(magazine)" title="Guitarist (magazine)">Guitarist</a></i> in 2004: "I don't think anyone has epitomised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riff#Riff" title="Riff">riff</a> writing better than <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a> â he's one of the great brains of rock music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> May was also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Hackett" title="Steve Hackett">Steve Hackett</a>, guitarist of <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> in particular his harmony guitar solo at the end of the band's epic 1971 song "<a href="/wiki/The_Musical_Box_(Genesis_song)" title="The Musical Box (Genesis song)">The Musical Box</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>While May and his father were building the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>, May also produced plans to build a second guitar. However, so successful was the Red Special, that May had no need to build another guitar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Spade_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Spade-100">[100]</a></sup> These plans were eventually given to guitar <a href="/wiki/Luthier" title="Luthier">luthier</a> Andrew Guyton in around 2004/05, some slight modifications were made and the guitar was built. It was named "The Spade", as the shape of the body resembled the form shown on playing cards. However the guitar also came to be known as "The Guitar That Time Forgot".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Spade_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Spade-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Guitars_and_keyboards">Guitars and keyboards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Guitars and keyboards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Most of May's electric guitar work live and in the studio was done on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>, which he built with his father, an electronics engineer, during his teenage years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> From 1975 onwards, he has also had some replicas made, some of which were also used for live and recording purposes, others were mainly spares. The most famous replicas were made by John Birch in 1975 (May actually smashed it during a concert in the States in 1982), <a href="/wiki/Greco_guitars" title="Greco guitars">Greco</a> BM90 (featured in the promo video of "Good Old-Fashioned Lover Boy" in 1977), Guild (back-up from 1984 to 1993), Fryers (1997â1998, used both live and in the studio) and Guyton<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> (back-up from 2003 to present). On stage, May used to carry at least one back-up guitar (in case he broke a string) and occasionally would use others for certain songs or parts, such as alternate tunings. Currently, May owns a company which makes guitars whose design is modelled after the original Red Special guitar.</p>
<ul>
<li>July 1973Â â May 1974: <a href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster" title="Fender Stratocaster">Fender Stratocaster</a> CBS era (thought to be a 1972)</li>
<li>October 1974Â â May 1975: <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Gibson Les Paul</a> Deluxe, and the Stratocaster from the previous tour.</li>
<li>November 1975Â â May 1976: Same two guitars as before, plus a natural finish John Birch replica of the Red Special.</li>
<li>September 1976: Same three as before, plus a Martin D-18 acoustic for "'39".</li>
<li>January 1977Â â August 1979: Just the Birch replica plus an Ovation Pacemaker 12-string acoustic on some numbers ("'39", "Love of My Life", "Dreamer's Ball").</li>
<li>November 1979Â â June 1982: Birch replica (back-up), <a href="/wiki/Fender_Telecaster" title="Fender Telecaster">Fender Telecaster</a> ("Crazy Little Thing Called Love" 2ndÂ verse, middle-eight and solo), Ovation (acoustic numbers).</li>
<li>JulyÂ â November 1982: Added a <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Flying_V" title="Gibson Flying V">Gibson Flying V</a> as second back-up. On 9 August 1982 Brian smashed the Birch guitar, so the FlyingÂ V became the only spare.</li>
<li>AugustÂ â October 1984: The Flying V became a second back-up again as his main spare was the Guild replica. He also used Roger Taylor's Gibson Chet-Atkins Classical Electric.</li>
<li>July 1985Â â August 1986: Gibson Flying V no longer used. The rest remained the same.</li>
<li>In 2012 he received a double-neck replica of the Red Special with the second neck having 12-strings. He used this guitar at a few gigs with <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> now being able to play the 12-string part from the studio version of Under Pressure live.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Double-neck_Red_Special_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Double-neck_Red_Special-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>He currently has a Guild 12-string to replace his Ovation Pacemaker. Some of the non-RS electric guitars he used in the studio included:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burns_London" title="Burns London">Burns</a> Double Six on "Long Away" (1976) and "Under Pressure" (1981).</li>
<li>Fender Telecaster on "Crazy Little Thing Called Love" (1979). It was used for the video (but not the recordings) of "Back Chat" (1982).</li>
<li>Gibson Firebird on "Hammer to Fall" and "Tear It Up" (album versions only, not on stage).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ibanez_JS_Series" title="Ibanez JS Series">Ibanez JS</a> on "Nothing But Blue" (1991).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Parker_Fly" title="Parker Fly">Parker Fly</a> on "Mother Love" (1993â1995).</li>
</ul>
<p>For acoustic, he favoured Ovation, Martin, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C5%8Dkai_Guitars" title="TÅkai Guitars">TÅkai</a> Hummingbird, Godin and Guild. On a couple of videos he also used some different electric guitars: a Stratocaster copy on "Play the Game" (1980) and a <a href="/wiki/Washburn_RR-V_Tour_Series" title="Washburn RR-V Tour Series">Washburn RR2V</a> on "Princes of the Universe" (1986).</p>
<p>In 1984 <a href="/wiki/Guild_Guitar_Company" title="Guild Guitar Company">Guild</a> released the first official Red Special replica for mass production, and made some prototypes specifically for May. However the solid body construction (the original RS has hollow cavities in the body) and the pick-ups (DiMarzio) that were not an exact replica of the Burns TriSonic did not make May happy, so the production stopped after just 300Â guitars. In 1993 Guild made a second replica of the RS, made in just 1000Â copies, of which May has some and used as a back-up. At the moment, he uses the two guitars made by Greg Fryerâthe luthier who restored the Old Lady in 1998âas back-up. They are almost identical to the original, except for the Fryer logo on the headstock (May's original one has a sixpence).</p>
