<p>In the studio, May used <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_DX7" title="Yamaha DX7">Yamaha DX7</a> synths for the opening sequence of "<a href="/wiki/One_Vision" title="One Vision">One Vision</a>" and the backgrounds of "<a href="/wiki/Who_Wants_to_Live_Forever" title="Who Wants to Live Forever">Who Wants to Live Forever</a>" (also on stage), "<a href="/wiki/Scandal_(song)" title="Scandal (song)">Scandal</a>" and <a href="/wiki/The_Show_Must_Go_On_(Queen_song)" title="The Show Must Go On (Queen song)">"The Show Must Go On"</a>. He mostly used Freddie Mercury's 1972 Steinway piano and reportedly now owns the instrument in question. May was keen on using some toys as instruments as well. He used a <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_Corporation" title="Yamaha Corporation">Yamaha</a> plastic piano in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teo_Torriatte" title="Teo Torriatte">Teo Torriatte</a>" and a toy mini <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koto_(musical_instrument)" title="Koto (musical instrument)">koto</a> in <a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">"The Prophet's Song"</a>. He also used a "genuine George Formby Ukulele-Banjo" in "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bring_Back_That_Leroy_Brown" title="Bring Back That Leroy Brown">Bring Back That Leroy Brown</a>" and <a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">"Good Company"</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Amplifiers_and_effects">Amplifiers and effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Amplifiers and effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>May has used <a href="/wiki/Vox_AC30" title="Vox AC30">Vox AC30</a> amplifiers almost exclusively since a meeting with his long-time hero <a href="/wiki/Rory_Gallagher" title="Rory Gallagher">Rory Gallagher</a> at a gig in London during the late 1960s/early 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In the mid-1970s he used six of them, with an <a href="/wiki/Echoplex" title="Echoplex">Echoplex</a> delay (with extended delay time) plugged into a separate amplifier, and a second Echoplex plugged into yet another amp; he used a homemade booster, his only effects pedal, which was on all the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reply_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-reply-107">[107]</a></sup> His choice is the model AC30TBX, the top-boost version with Blue Alnico speakers, and he runs the amp at full volume on the Normal channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> He also customises his amps by removing the circuitry for the Brilliant and Vib-trem channels (leaving only the circuitry for the Normal), and this alters the tone slightly, with a gain addition of 6â7Â dB. He always used a <a href="/wiki/Treble_booster" title="Treble booster">treble booster</a> which, along with the AC30 and his custom '<a href="/wiki/Deacy_Amp" title="Deacy Amp">Deacy Amp</a>' transistor amp, built by Queen bass player John Deacon, went a long way in helping to create many of his signature guitar tones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> He used the Dallas Rangemaster for the first Queen albums, up to <i><a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_(album)" title="A Day at the Races (album)">A Day at the Races</a></i>. Effects guru <a href="/wiki/Pete_Cornish" title="Pete Cornish">Pete Cornish</a> built for him the TB-83 (32Â dB of gain) that was used for all the remaining Queen albums. He switched in 2000 to the Fryer's booster, which actually gives less boost than the TB-83.</p>
<p>When performing live, he uses banks of Vox AC30 amplifiers keeping some amps with only guitar and others with all effects such as delay, flanger and chorus. He has a rack of 14Â AC30s, which are grouped as Normal, Chorus, DelayÂ 1, DelayÂ 2. On his pedal board, May has a custom switch unit made by Cornish and subsequently modified by Fryer that allows him to choose which amps are active. He uses a <a href="/wiki/Boss_Corporation" title="Boss Corporation">BOSS</a> pedal from the '70s, the Chorus Ensemble CE-1, which can be heard in "<a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack" title="Sheer Heart Attack">In The Lap of The Gods</a>" (<i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Wembley_%2786" title="Live at Wembley '86">Live at Wembley '86</a></i>) or "<a href="/wiki/Hammer_to_Fall" title="Hammer to Fall">Hammer to Fall</a>" (slow version played live with P.Â Rodgers). Next in the chain, he uses a Foxx Foot Phaser ("We Will Rock You", "We Are the Champions", "Keep Yourself Alive", etc.), and two delay machines to play his trademark solo in "Brighton Rock".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1073" data-file-width="750" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg/220px-Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg/330px-Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg/440px-Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_Portrait_-_David_J_Cable.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May in 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1974 to 1988, May was married to Chrissie Mullen and they had three children: James (aka Jimmy), born on 15 June 1978; Louisa, born on 22 May 1981 and Emily Rose, born on 18 February 1987. May and Chrissie separated in 1988. He met <i><a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a></i> actress <a href="/wiki/Anita_Dobson" title="Anita Dobson">Anita Dobson</a> in 1986; she inspired him to write the 1989 hit "I Want It All". They married on 18 November 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>He has stated in interviews that he suffered from severe depression in the late 1980s and early 1990s, to the point of contemplating suicide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> for reasons having to do with his troubled first marriage, his perceived failure as a husband and a father, his father Harold's death and Freddie Mercury's illness and death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>May's father Harold worked as a <a href="/wiki/Drafter" title="Drafter">draughtsman</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Aviation" title="Ministry of Aviation">Ministry of Aviation</a> and was a long-time heavy cigarette smoker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grdn2014_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Grdn2014-10">[10]</a></sup> As a result, May dislikes smoking,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> even to the point where he has prohibited smoking indoors at his more recent concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> According to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times_(UK)" title="The Sunday Times (UK)">The Sunday Times</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List" title="Sunday Times Rich List">Rich List</a> he is worth Â£85Â million or around $135 million as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brian May is a vegetarian. He has homes in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windlesham" title="Windlesham">Windlesham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> He is an active <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> advocate, and was appointed a vice-president of animal welfare charity, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RSPCA" title="RSPCA">RSPCA</a>, in September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Astrophysics">Astrophysics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Astrophysics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="1280" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg/220px-Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg/330px-Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg/440px-Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rock_Star_and_Astrophysicist_Brian_May_Visits_Paranal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May in 2015 at <a href="/wiki/Paranal_Observatory" title="Paranal Observatory">Paranal Observatory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May studied physics and mathematics at <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, graduating with a BSc (Hons) degree and <a href="/wiki/Associate_of_the_Royal_College_of_Science" title="Associate of the Royal College of Science">ARCS</a> in physics with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second-class_honours" title="Second-class honours">Upper Second-Class Honours</a>. From 1970 to 1974, he studied for a PhD degree at Imperial College, studying reflected light from interplanetary dust and the velocity of dust in the plane of the Solar System. When Queen started to have international success in 1974, he abandoned his doctoral studies, but co-authored two scientific research papers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> which were based on his observations at the <a href="/wiki/Teide_Observatory" title="Teide Observatory">Teide Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>.</p>
<p>In October 2006, May re-registered for his PhD at Imperial College and submitted his thesis in August 2007 (one year earlier than he estimated it would take to complete). As well as writing up the previous work he had done, May had to review the work on zodiacal dust undertaken during the intervening 33 years, which included the discovery of the zodiacal dust bands by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/IRAS" title="IRAS">IRAS</a> satellite. After a <a href="/wiki/Oral_exam" title="Oral exam">viva voce</a>, the revised thesis (entitled <i>A Survey of Radial Velocities in the Zodiacal Dust Cloud</i>) was approved in September 2007, some 37 years after it had been commenced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buzzcocksphd_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-buzzcocksphd-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> He was able to submit his thesis only because of the minimal amount of research on the topic during the intervening years and has described the subject as one that became "trendy" again in the 2000s. He graduated at the awards ceremony of Imperial College held in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> on 14 May 2008.</p>
<p>In October 2007, May was appointed a Visiting Researcher in Imperial College and continues his interest in astronomy and involvement with the Imperial Astrophysics Group.</p>
<p>He is co-author, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Patrick_Moore" title="Sir Patrick Moore">Sir Patrick Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Lintott" title="Chris Lintott">Chris Lintott</a>, of <i>Bang! â The Complete History of the Universe</i> (published in 2006)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> and "The Cosmic Tourist" (published in 2012).</p>
<p>Asteroid <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/52665_Brianmay" title="52665 Brianmay">52665 Brianmay</a> was named in his honour on 18 June 2008 on the suggestion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Patrick_Moore" title="Sir Patrick Moore">Sir Patrick Moore</a> (probably influenced by the asteroid's provisional designation of <span class="nowrap">1998 <b>BM</b><sub>30</sub></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rdspecial_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-rdspecial-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, May co-founded <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_Day" title="Asteroid Day">Asteroid Day</a> with <a href="/wiki/Apollo_9" title="Apollo 9">Apollo 9</a> astronaut <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Schweickart" title="Rusty Schweickart">Rusty Schweickart</a>, <a href="/wiki/B612_Foundation" title="B612 Foundation">B612 Foundation</a> COO Danica Remy and German filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Grigorij_Richters" title="Grigorij Richters">Grigorij Richters</a>. <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_Day" title="Asteroid Day">Asteroid Day</a> is a global awareness campaign where people from around the world come together to learn about asteroids and what we can do to protect our planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>May appeared on the 700th episode of <a href="/wiki/The_Sky_at_Night" title="The Sky at Night">The Sky at Night</a> hosted by Sir Patrick Moore, along with Chris Lintott, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Culshaw" title="Jon Culshaw">Jon Culshaw</a>, Prof. <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cox_(physicist)" title="Brian Cox (physicist)">Brian Cox</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Astronomer_Royal" title="Astronomer Royal">Astronomer Royal</a> <a href="/wiki/Martin_Rees" title="Martin Rees">Martin Rees</a> who on departing the panel, told Brian May, who was joining it, "I don't know a scientist who looks as much like <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> as you do".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian-2011_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-2011-127">[127]</a></sup> May was also a guest on the first episode of the third series of the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Stargazing_Live" title="Stargazing Live">Stargazing Live</a></i>, on 8 January 2013.</p>
<p>On 17 November 2007, May was appointed Chancellor of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_John_Moores_University" title="Liverpool John Moores University">Liverpool John Moores University</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Chancellor_confirmed_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Chancellor_confirmed-128">[128]</a></sup> and installed in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May_installed_as_uni_chancellor_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-May_installed_as_uni_chancellor-129">[129]</a></sup> He held the post until 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian-2011_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-2011-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a> Pluto flyby NASA press conference held on 17 July 2015 at Johns Hopkins Applied Physics Lab, Brian May was introduced as a science team collaborator. He told the panel "You have inspired the world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activism">Activism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Activism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="347" data-file-width="317" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg/220px-Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f3/Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brian_May_filming_for_the_BBC%27s_%27The_One_Show%27.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
May filming for the BBC's <i>The One Show</i> in 2011 for an anti badger culling campaign.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>May has formed a group to promote animal welfare. Though a <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> voter most of his life,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> he has stated that their policies on <a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">fox hunting</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Culling" title="Culling">culling</a> of <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badgers</a> meant he did not vote for them at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 General Election</a>. His group, <a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(animal_welfare)" title="Save Me (animal welfare)">Save Me</a> (named after <a href="/wiki/Save_Me_(Queen_song)" title="Save Me (Queen song)">the May-written Queen song</a>), campaigns for the protection of all animals against unnecessary, cruel and degrading treatment; with a particular emphasis on preventing hunting of foxes and the culling of badgers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animal_rights_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-animal_rights-9">[9]</a></sup> The group's primary concern is to ensure that the <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Act_2004" title="Hunting Act 2004">Hunting Act 2004</a> and other laws protecting animals are retained in situ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-save-me.org.uk_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-save-me.org.uk-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview in September 2010 with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sackur" title="Stephen Sackur">Stephen Sackur</a> for the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/HARDtalk" title="HARDtalk">HARDtalk</a></i> program, May said that he would rather be remembered for his animal rights work than for his music or scientific work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> May is a staunch supporter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RSPCA" title="RSPCA">RSPCA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Fund_for_Animal_Welfare" title="International Fund for Animal Welfare">International Fund for Animal Welfare</a>, the <a href="/wiki/League_Against_Cruel_Sports" title="League Against Cruel Sports">League Against Cruel Sports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PETA_UK" title="PETA UK">PETA UK</a> and the Harper Asprey Wildlife Rescue.</p>
<p>In March 2012, May contributed the foreword to a target paper published by the think tank the <a href="/wiki/Bow_Group" title="Bow Group">Bow Group</a>, urging the government to reconsider its plans to cull thousands of badgers to control <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bovine_TB" title="Bovine TB">bovine TB</a>, stating that the findings of Labour's major badger culling trials, several years earlier, show that culling does not work. The paper was authored by Graham Godwin-Pearson with contributions by leading <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> scientists, including <a href="/wiki/John_Krebs,_Baron_Krebs" title="John Krebs, Baron Krebs">Lord Krebs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Brian May joined French guitar player <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Danel" title="Jean-Pierre Danel">Jean-Pierre Danel</a> for a charity Danel launched to the benefit of animal rights in France. The guitarists signed guitars and art photos together, and were joined by <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2013, May teamed up with actor <a href="/wiki/Brian_Blessed" title="Brian Blessed">Brian Blessed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flash_animation" title="Flash animation">Flash</a> cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Jonti_Picking" title="Jonti Picking">Jonti "Weebl" Picking</a>, as well as animal rights groups including the RSPCA, to form Team Badger, a "coalition of organisations that have teamed up to fight the planned cull of badgers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> With Weebl and Blessed, May recorded a single, '"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Save_The_Badger_Badger_Badger" title="Save The Badger Badger Badger">Save The Badger Badger Badger</a>'" â a <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mashup</a> of Weebl's viral 2003 Flash cartoon <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">meme</a>, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badger_Badger_Badger" title="Badger Badger Badger">Badger Badger Badger</a>", and Queen's "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_(song)" title="Flash (song)">Flash</a>", featuring vocals by Blessed. Weebl animated <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EllYgcWmcAY" rel="nofollow"><span class="plainlinks">the music video</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, parodying both Weebl's <a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EIyixC9NsLI" rel="nofollow"><span class="plainlinks">original animation</span></a> on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> and a scene from <i><a href="/wiki/Flash_Gordon_(film)" title="Flash Gordon (film)">Flash Gordon</a></i>, a film featuring music by Queen, and in which Blessed played Prince Vultan. On 1 September 2013, "Save The Badger Badger Badger" charted at No. 79 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>, No. 39 on the UK <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> chart<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalspy_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspy-139">[139]</a></sup> and No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> Rock chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian-140">[140]</a></sup> In June 2013 renowned naturalist <a href="/wiki/David_Attenborough" title="David Attenborough">David Attenborough</a> and rock guitarist <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a> joined May to form the supergroup, Artful Badger and Friends, and released a song dedicated to badgers, "Badger Swagger".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>, it was reported that May was considering standing as an <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independent Member of Parliament</a>. It was also revealed that May had started a "Common Decency" project "to re-establish common decency in our lives, work and Parliament". May said he wanted to "get rid of the current government" and wished to see a <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> containing "individuals voting according to their conscience".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> May was one of several celebrities who endorsed the parliamentary candidacy of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a> at the election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> He also endorsed a Conservative Party candidate, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Smith_(British_politician)" title="Henry Smith (British politician)">Henry Smith</a>, on the grounds of his animal welfare record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2015, May criticized British prime minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> for giving Members of Parliament a free vote on amending the ban on fox hunting in England and Wales. During a live television interview, he also attacked the pro-hunting organisation the <a href="/wiki/Countryside_Alliance" title="Countryside Alliance">Countryside Alliance</a> as "a bunch of lying bastards" for their support for a change to the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The vote was postponed by the government following the intervention of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>'s Westminster MPs, who committed to vote to keep the ban as it existed. May told anti-hunt protesters in a rally outside Parliament that it was "a very, very important day for our democracy" but added "we have not yet won the war, there's no room for complacency".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>A new damselfly species of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Heteragrion" title="Heteragrion">Heteragrion</a></i> (OdonataÂ : Zygoptera) from Brazil was named <i>Heteragrion brianmayi</i> in honour of him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stereophotography">Stereophotography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_May&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Stereophotography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>May has had a lifelong interest in collecting Victorian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stereophotography" title="Stereophotography">stereophotography</a>. In 2009, with co-author Elena Vidal, he published his second book, <i><a href="/wiki/A_Village_Lost_and_Found" title="A Village Lost and Found">A Village Lost and Found</a>,</i> on the work of English stereophotography innovator <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Richard_Williams" title="Thomas Richard Williams">T. R. Williams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> He was awarded The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Photographic_Society" title="Royal Photographic Society">Royal Photographic Society</a>'s Saxby Medal in 2012 for achievement in the field of three-dimensional imaging.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>May made a significant technical contribution to the book to accompany the exhibition 'Stereoscopic Photographs of Pablo Picasso by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mouzillat" title="Robert Mouzillat">Robert Mouzillat</a>', held at the <a href="/wiki/Holburne_Museum" title="Holburne Museum">Holburne Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bath,_Somerset" title="Bath, Somerset">Bath</a>, UK from February to June 2014. The book provides a cross-section of photographs of Picasso in his studio, at the bullfight at <a href="/wiki/Arles" title="Arles">Arles</a> and in his garden. May's 3D 'Owl viewer' is used to view the photographs in 3D.</p>
<p>The purchase of his first card in 1973 started May on a lifelong and worldwide search for <a href="/wiki/Les_Diableries" title="Les Diableries">Les Diableries</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> which are stereoscopic photographs depicting scenes of daily life in Hell. On 10 October 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> the book <i>Diableries: Stereoscopic Adventures in Hell</i> by Brian May, Denis Pellerin and Paula Fleming was published.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
